Local Duplex Silk Factories Had Been Closed for Over Ten Days Caused by The Weakening European Sales. Now, The Representatives Returning from Beijing Stated that The Government Had Agrees to Give Aid to the Factories. It’s Believed that Bond For The Public Silk Factories is Approved. This Means That The Silk Factories Are Preparing To Be Opened Which Will Increase The Demand For Cocoons Significantly. The Price For Cocoons Would Most Likely Increase By Four Or Five Taels. Wuxi Double-Cocooned Silk at The Guilds Were Worth Forty-Eight Taels, But No Trades Were Closed

Black and Green Tea Sales To Russia Continue 111

Yesterday, Local Tea Firms and Foreign Firms Continued Selling Red Tea From Keemun and Green Tea From Gong Xi to The Russians. However, The Sales Price Remains Low and Merchants Incurr Great Losses. Fine Green Tea, Tian Xiang, Xing Cheng etc. has Received Some Orders and The Prices have increased To One Hundred Thirty-Five Taels. Otherwise Trades Are Slow. Chinese Tea Trade Relationship Is Grim

Oil Market: White Tung Oil Gradually Entering a Favorable Situation 112

Large quantities of Xiang Tung Oil are being transported to Wuhan. The price of White Tung Oil Has Rebounded After The Falling Of Tung Oil. Several Foreign Firms Inquired Prices After A Steady Decrease In Prices. Over the Last Two Days, The Amount of Wuhan Shanghai Trading Had reached Seven Hundred Tons Priced From Sixteen Point Five Taels and Eighteen Taels. However, Degree Oil Remain Dull Priced at Twenty-Seven Yuans. At This Time With Constant Upward Price Fluctuation. At The Afternoon, Large Quantities of Xiang Tong Oils Were Heard to be transported straight To Hubei. Whether Prices Will Rebound or Decline is Under Intense Debate

Cloth Trade: Flat And Thick Clothes Sells Quite Well 113

The Sales of Flat And Thick Clothes Are Quite high Because As the weather get Cold, Overcoat Stores Have Increased Their Requisitions. The Resale Market Is Very Good. The Price for Thaiho’s 101 has Reached Forty Two and a Half Kilos. For Ruifeng, The Initial Quality Is Five Taels while the lower quality is Two point Five Six. All Of Huabo Is Two Point Eight Taels. Silver Colored Are more Expensive Because it is Lower In Quantities than The Original Color

Metal and Brass: English Steel Plate Prices Crashes Thirty-Four Cents 114

There Were Several English Steel Plates The Comes In, The Overall Supply Is More Than the Demands. Thus, It Caused Panic for The Buyer, Who Wants Cheaper Price to be Listed. The Current Price is Now: Two Point Five Percent - Nine Point Two and a Half Taels; A Portion - Six Point Seven Taels; Seven Point Five Percent - Six Point Two and a Half Taels; One Part - Five Point Nine and A Half Taels; A Decrease of Thirty to Forty Cents Compared With Market Prices.

Today is the Anniversary of the Premier's Birthday 168

Celebration Held in the Morning, Entertainment Performed in the Afternoon. Today is the 65th Anniversary of the Birthday of Dr. Sun Yat-sen, the Premier of the Chinese Nationalist Party. The Japanese Municipal Executive Committee has specially convened representatives from various organizations, groups, schools, and party branches at all levels to hold a commemorative meeting at the Gonghe Cinema on Minguo Road, South City, at 9:00 a.m. today. In the afternoon, entertainment will be performed at the Municipal Chamber of Commerce. All sectors will display flags and close for one day to celebrate. The township areas will also hold commemorative ceremonies separately. The Municipal Executive Committee issued a notice to comrades yesterday, saying:

Today's Launching Ceremony of the Yixian Warship 169

Designed According to the Latest Cruiser Design, the Seafarers Party Branch Issues a Notice to Fellow Compatriots. The Naval Department's Yixian warship is scheduled to hold a launching ceremony at 4:00 p.m. today. The Central Party Headquarters and the National Government have dispatched Commander Xiong Shihui of the Songhu Garrison to deliver a speech on behalf of the party, and Ms. Chen Shuying, the wife of Sun Zhesheng, has been invited to perform the bottle-breaking ceremony. Vice Minister Chen Shaokuan of the Naval Department came to Shanghai the day before yesterday to preside over all matters, and Chief of General Affairs Li Shijia and others also came to Shanghai yesterday morning. A summary of various aspects is provided below:

Today's Launching Ceremony of the Yixian Warship 170

Order of Ceremony: (1) All take their seats; (2) Play music and sing the Party Anthem; (4) All bow three times to the National Party Flag and the Premier's Portrait; (5) The Chairman respectfully reads the Premier's Will; (6) Play music; (7) Conduct the Launching Ceremony; (8) The Chairman delivers the opening remarks; (9) The Representative of the Central Party Headquarters delivers an address; (10) The Representative of the National Government delivers an address; (11) The Representative of the Executive Yuan delivers an address; (12) Guests deliver speeches; (13) The Chairman responds; (14) Shout slogans; (15) Ceremony concludes; (16) Play music; (17) Take photographs; (18) Refreshments.

A Glimpse of the Ceremony Venue: The ceremony venue is on the right side of the Jiangnan Shipyard. A wooden platform was erected yesterday. The Naval Special Party Branch and the Naval Compilation Office were busy decorating everything. Both sides are filled with naval flags and slogans of various countries. In the center are the Party and National Flags and the Premier's portrait. In front of the platform is the bow of the Yixian warship, facing the platform, with a silver-gray hull and a reddish-brown bottom. It is larger than the Minquan and Yongshui warships, so the uppermost part of the bow protrudes beyond the top of the platform. Workers are busy with painting and other tasks. Vice Minister Chen Shaokuan of the Naval Department, Chief of General Affairs Li Shijia, and Chief of the Management Section Chen Jingxiang also inspected and provided instructions at the ceremony platform yesterday afternoon.

Various Aspects of the Yixian: The keel of the Yixian warship was laid on April 10th of this year and is scheduled to be completed in March of the 20th year [of the Republic, i.e., 1931]. The construction cost is estimated at 2.8 million yuan. The chief supervisor is Li Shijia, Chief of the General Affairs Department of the Naval Department. The supervisors are Wang Zhiguang, Lin Huiping, Chen Yaoping, Gao Chunmao, Gai Bangyue, etc. The warship is a light cruiser and will be assigned to the First Fleet. It is 270 feet long, 34 feet wide, and has a displacement of 1,550 tons. Its armament includes two 6-inch caliber guns, four 3-inch anti-aircraft guns, two 6-pound guns, and eight machine guns. Its coal capacity is 300 tons, its speed is 20 nautical miles per hour, and its cruising range is over 2,000 nautical miles. The crew consists of 160 personnel, and the captain is of the rank of lieutenant colonel. It is also equipped with the latest cruiser design, including accurate navigation instruments, combat command instruments, long and short-wave wireless telegraphs, wireless telephones, and powerful searchlights.

A Notice to Fellow Compatriots: As long as international wars cannot be absolutely eliminated, armaments are indispensable. Now, the scope of warfare, in addition to the mainland, requires a balanced development of naval, land, and air preparations. Although we cannot harbor any intention of aggression, passive self-defense must be the minimum preparation for an independent country. At present, our country's self-defense capabilities are far from our ideal standards, so we are not seeking freedom and equality, but the equipment of considerable military strength. Who can say that it is not a factual requirement? Just take naval defense as an example. From the mouth of the Yalu River in Andong, Liaoning, to the Beilun Estuary in Qinzhou, Guangdong, including more than 10,000 miles of coastline in the seven provinces of Liaoning, Hebei, Shandong, Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Fujian, and Guangdong, the navy used to defend it has less than 50,000 tons and less than 100 ships. This is a problem that deserves the painstaking thought of our compatriots across the country in order to solve it. Since the National Revolutionary Army unified the country, our party has followed the Premier's will and strived for China's freedom and equality, first eliminating the rebels across the country to realize political tutelage. The naval authorities have adhered to this goal. In addition to participating in the anti-rebel work, they have also actively sought the development of naval construction. The Xianning, Yongshui, and Minquan warships have been completed previously, the Yixian warship was launched on the Premier's birthday, and the Minsheng warship has also begun construction. Under the current economic situation of extreme exhaustion, there are not many quantities and powerful constructions in fact, but the authorities' painstaking plans should win the sympathy and support of compatriots across the country. It is hoped that warships will continue to be launched in the future, and the tonnage will gradually increase to lay the groundwork for reaching our self-defense goals first. Dear compatriots, the need for the navy in our country and its past weakness are known to everyone. The launching of the Yixian warship can only be regarded as a meager supplement to healing this weakness. It is still hoped that everyone's enthusiasm will support and promote the continuous construction, so that this weak person can repeatedly have a large number of supplements and become strong, as a healthy maritime guarantee for our Chinese nation. Finally, our slogans are: Increase naval construction, consolidate our coastal defense! The Executive Committee of the Naval Special Party Branch.

Silk Factory Agreement to Resume Production 171

Agreement Reached to Reduce Wages and Strive to Resume Production; 32 Factories Expected to Resume Production Before the 15th

The Shanghai Silk Factory Association stated that each factory had suffered drastic losses due to plummeting European sales, making it impossible to sustain operations. Consequently, except for Doung Gong silk factories and those already shut down, all 106 silk factories in Shanghai uniformly ceased operations at the end of last month. Over the past ten days, the livelihoods of more than 100,000 workers have been increasingly imperiled, resulting in a grave situation. As the representatives who went to Beijing to petition have now returned to Shanghai, an emergency meeting was convened for all industry members yesterday (the 11th) at 3 PM. Attendees included standing committee members Zhu Jing'an, Huang Jinfan, Zhang Peishen, Wang Xiaolai, and representatives from 93 silk factories, totaling about 100 individuals. Chairman Shen Huachen opened the meeting with customary rituals.

First, Wang Xiaolai (one of the petitioning representatives) reported on the petitioning process in Beijing, stating that the nine representatives from the three provinces and cities of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Shanghai first went to the National Government and the Executive Yuan on the morning of the 3rd, where they were met by secretaries. Then, they went to the Ministry of Finance, where they were received by Vice Minister Li Tiaosheng. The Ministry of Industry and Commerce was visited and personally received by Minister Kong, where each representative detailed the decline in European silk sales and the immense losses sustained by silk factories. The factories, unable to support themselves, had successively shut down throughout Shanghai, verging on bankruptcy. They requested that the government issue 10 million yuan in Jiangsu-Zhejiang-Shanghai silk industry public bonds within the year to provide relief. Ministers Li and Kong both agreed to do their utmost to find a way to comply. In Beijing, they hosted banquets for various heads of government agencies. As of yet, no official order has been issued, and a decision has not been made. They will go to Beijing again tomorrow to present a follow-up report. The report was followed by a proposal to discuss

The Issue of Resuming Production.

Manufacturers successively rose to report on the reasons for the shutdown: (1) European and American silk sales had reached an extreme point of stagnation, with silk prices being extraordinarily low. The cost of silk production was relatively high, resulting in a loss of over 200 taels of silver per bale of silk sold, depleting all capital. (2) Excessive burdens made it increasingly difficult to sustain operations. Thus, silk factories had no choice but to halt production. Chairman Shen stated, "Our country's manufactured silk is its largest foreign trade commodity. If all silk factories shut down, the silk market will stagnate. Our colleagues should find ways to maintain the inherent business of China's silk industry. I urge my colleagues to find ways to resume production as soon as possible to sustain the livelihoods of over 100,000 workers. As for reducing wages to alleviate the burden, the association is hesitant to propose this. Even if wages are reduced, without a source of raw materials, it will be difficult to resume production. What will we say in response to external criticisms? Moreover, it's easy to reduce wages but difficult to increase them. Workers may not be happy with this."

Subsequently, manufacturers from areas such as Hongkou reported that their district's silk factories had convened a joint labor-management meeting on the 7th of this month to discuss wage reductions. Workers understood the severe losses suffered by factories due to stagnant European silk sales, high costs, and low prices, and were very understanding of the difficult business conditions. They were willing to accept wage reductions, with all female workers' wages, staff salaries, and silkworm moth subsidies being paid at 80% of the original amount. Once the selling price of medium-grade silk reached over 1,000 taels, the original amount would be restored. Currently, factories were willing to pay female workers, who previously received 60 cents per day, 50 cents instead of the 48 cents after the 20% reduction. Workers in other districts, having been out of work for an extended period, expressed similar sentiments to help factories resume production as soon as possible.

The chairman then stated that the purpose of today's meeting was to discuss the resumption of production, focusing on whether or not it was possible. The issue of wage reductions should be addressed by each district convening its own labor-management meeting, working together in good faith. Those colleagues who could resume production immediately were asked to stand. At that time, only four factories stood: Fengtai (Zhabei District), Xinchang (Caojiadu), Lunyuan Fushen (Xinzha District), etc. The remaining Shunfeng (Zhabei District) and Anfeng (Xinzha) would restart machines tomorrow; Xiechang and Xiexing (Xinzha), Yingyu Fumin Baishi No. 1 and Baishi No. 2 (Zhabei) would restart on the 13th; Yufeng on the 14th; and Xinglun on the 15th. As for Yuanfeng (Hongkou), Xie'an (Zhabei), Tongwei Yujing (Hongkou), Jinyun (Xinzha), Yichang (Hongkou), Rui Heyu Kangxu and Lunxiang Qingfeng Hengkang Ruifengyu (Xinzha), Yongan Tongyi Qichang, etc., they needed to make preparations before choosing a date to resume production. Seven Doung Gong silk factories, except for Yonglun, would resume production today. Finally, representatives from the 32 silk factories that were resuming production continued to meet to discuss the procedures. It was resolved that workers' wages would be paid at 80% across the board. The workers would be notified of the resumption date in advance by the car operators. A notice detailing the losses incurred by the factories, necessitating compliance with the proposal to temporarily reduce wages for both male and female staff by 20%, would be posted in front of the factory. Female workers receiving 60 cents in wages would be paid 50 cents, and worker allowances, silkworm moth subsidies, etc., would be paid at 80% of the original amount to ensure everyone was aware. The meeting adjourned at 7 PM.

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Petitions to Change Year-End Closing Period 172

Set for the Day Before the Start of Spring Each Year

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce submitted a petition to the Bureau of Social Affairs yesterday, requesting a change to the year-end closing date, stating that the current date poses difficulties for both agricultural and commercial circumstances. The petition, made on behalf of various trade associations, requested to change the year-end closing date to the day before the Start of Spring (Lichun Festival), to accommodate both the implementation of the national calendar and commercial considerations. The petition stated:

"Last year, the Commercial Consolidation Committee deliberated on amending the handling of merchants' accounts to adopt the national calendar, resolving to designate the end of May and the end of December of the national calendar as the closing periods. This was approved and submitted to the National Government for implementation nationwide. This year, the ends of May and September were handled accordingly. However, since the year-end closing date is very close, and because various industries have foreign account relationships, and since this is the initial implementation, preparations must be made in advance to avoid delays. The association issued early warnings and announcements to remind various industries. The Money Trade Association, the Coal Trade Association, and others also published notices urging foreign merchants to prepare early. On October 3rd, the association received a letter from the Hangzhou Chamber of Commerce stating that because this is the initial implementation, it is difficult for various counties to achieve uniformity. If debts must be paid on schedule at the end of the year, but debts owed to them cannot be recovered, it would inevitably lead to financial strain. They requested that the closing period be extended by one and a half months, and so on. The Local Tea Trade Association of this city submitted a letter stating the same. The association replied that since the implementation of the national calendar has been repeatedly ordered and the decision has been made, it is not appropriate to make further changes. At that time, 39 county chambers of commerce in Zhenjiang, Suzhou, and other places gathered in Zhenjiang, the capital of Jiangsu Province, and resolved to submit a joint petition to the Provincial Government and the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, stating that most of the new grain in the north and south of Jiangsu Province is still in the hands of farmers, and it is impossible to exchange grain for money to pay debts. It is impossible to close the accounts of rural stores, so how can the accounts of urban stores be settled? They requested to follow the example of the Jiangsu Province grain tax collection method, setting the deadline as the 16th day of the second month of the following year. The submitted draft was copied and sent for review. At the same time, the Bean and Rice Trade Association of this city also stated that new rice appears on the market in mid to late November, and the process of harvesting, drying, milling, and polishing rice from the countryside to the city and then to merchants cannot be completed in one or two months. Rice merchants must start accumulating stock between December and January. This is the time for various payments, not for collecting debts. They requested to set a separate accounting year for commercial affairs, with the end of January of the following year as the end of the previous year. Although this suggestion was rejected by your Bureau, various groups such as the Hat Shops, Fruit and Produce, Ginseng and Bird's Nest, Cosmetics, New Medicine, Shipping and Customs Clearance, Northern Goods, Firewood and Coal, and Paper Industries have all submitted letters stating their difficulties and requesting to review and change the method. The Wuhu General Chamber of Commerce also sent a letter to the association stating that commercial conditions there require a longer closing period and requested to convey this to silver and money industries, etc.

The association, occupying a leading position among merchants and acting as a conduit for communicating the hardships of merchants, must both implement national policies and not turn a blind eye to the difficulties faced by merchants. Since Jiangsu, Anhui, and Hangzhou have repeatedly expressed their concerns, and fearing that Shanghai's finances would be affected, the matter was brought up for discussion at the association's fifth standing committee meeting. Five inspectors were appointed to review the matter. The inspectors subsequently reported that although the decision to close accounts according to the national calendar cannot be changed, there is room to petition for modifying the date of the closing under the national calendar to better suit the needs of the business community. The inspectors noted that China is an agricultural country, and the national economy is tied to agricultural affairs. The association resolved that the previous dates of the end of May, the end of September, and the end of December for closing accounts were lacking in two aspects: (1) The original response to the Bureau of Social Affairs stated that the end of May was the time for silkworms and barley to appear on the market, and the end of September was the time for early rice to ripen. Both considered agricultural harvests, but the major closing period at the end of December did not. (2) If the end of December is the major closing period, then the first closing period from January 1st to the end of May is a full five months, the second closing period from June 1st to the end of September is four months, and the third closing period from October 1st to the end of December is only three months. This 5-4-3 system is too uneven. Although the Commercial Consolidation Committee had this method to wholeheartedly promote the national calendar, they had their own special difficulties. However, given the currently insurmountable difficulties that have arisen, it is necessary to seek remedies.

To remedy these practical difficulties, it is proposed to refer to the Bureau of Social Affairs' letter to the Commercial Consolidation Committee and divide the year into several periods according to the solar terms. The end of May, close to Lesser Fullness, and the end of September, close to Autumnal Equinox, should remain as the first and second closing periods. The commercial community's major closing period should be changed to the day before the Start of Spring each year. The reasons are as follows: (1) The Start of Spring is calculated according to the solar calendar and has no connection to the lunar calendar. (2) The Start of Spring is always on February 4th of the national calendar, and even if there is a change, it is on February 5th, differing by only one day. The dates can be calculated and determined. (3) Before the Start of Spring, agricultural harvests have long ended, and the income of farmers has been converted into cash. Whether in cities or towns, there are no issues with collecting and paying debts. (4) Setting February 4th as the major closing period would balance the lengths of the three closing periods, compensating for the excessive length of the first period and the excessive shortness of the second period. This was discussed at the association's sixteenth standing committee meeting on the 6th of this month and submitted to the sixth executive committee meeting. It was agreed that merchants' closing accounts are related to agricultural seasons, a point already understood by the municipal authorities. However, after reviewing the Bureau's rejection of the Bean and Rice Industry's petition, it was stated that the latest time for late rice to ripen is around the Frost's Descent solar term, and it has already been harvested. However, in reality, the majority of late rice has not yet been harvested after the Frost's Descent has already passed. Moreover, due to continuous rain, the weather has not cleared, and it is reported that late rice has been damaged and rice prices have risen. Therefore, the Bean and Rice Industry Association's statement that agricultural crops appear on the market in mid to late months is more accurate. As for changing the closing date of the commercial community to abolish the custom of the national calendar, the Start of Spring is on February 4th or 5th of the national calendar, with a fixed date. The national calendar New Year's Eve and the Start of Spring are not adjacent. Even taking this year as an example, there are more than ten days between them. Although the dates of the end of May and the end of September under the national calendar are not very far from the Dragon Boat Festival and the Mid-Autumn Festival, respectively, there is no risk of mistaking them as variations of the Dragon Boat Festival or the Mid-Autumn Festival. The reasons are the same. Moreover, Jiangsu Province also sets February 16th of the following year as the deadline for collecting grain taxes. Since the government must consider the capacity of the entire population when collecting taxes and does not limit the end of the year as the major closing date, there is no hindrance to the implementation of the national calendar within a reasonable range, and the deadline can be extended to avoid many conflicts and financial impacts. It was resolved to submit a request to the municipal authorities to forward it to the government for approval and record. This would be beneficial to the public. Respectfully submitted to the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs."

It is also reported that the association believes the closing issue needs to be resolved urgently as the end of the solar year is approaching and has separately sent a telegram to the State Council's Ministry of Industry and Commerce requesting approval and recording of this method.

Yesterday was the twelfth anniversary of the armistice of World War I. Consuls, naval and military officers from the former Allied countries in Shanghai, leaders of the Public Works Department and the Municipal Council of the two concessions, the International Chamber of Commerce, police officers, veterans, and relatives of the fallen gathered at the Peace Memorial Monument on the Bund outside Edward Road at 8:30 AM. Yesterday's Armistice Day Commemoration 175

Scene in front of the Peace Monument (photograph by this newspaper)

The General Headquarters for the Suppression of Bandits in Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui Ordered to Temporarily Postpone Dissolution 176

Continuing Past Achievements...Striving to Suppress Bandits

In May of this year, Xiong Shihui, the Songhu Garrison Commander, was ordered by Commander-in-Chief Chiang to concurrently take charge of bandit suppression affairs in the three provinces of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui. After assuming the position of General Commander, Xiong, recognizing the vastness and complexity of the three provinces, first initiated an investigation. Upon completion of the investigation, he convened a meeting of the bandit suppression officials from the three provinces to discuss bandit suppression plans. At that time, the military situation at the front was tense, and the number of troops available for bandit suppression was very limited. Xiong's 5th Division was also transferred to the front lines for combat. However, major bandit groups, such as Ma Yuren's gang in the Rugao and Yancheng areas of Jiangsu Province, Hu Gongmian's gang in the Wenchang and other regions of Zhejiang Province, Taibao Ashu's gang in the Jiahu and other regions, and Gao Jingqi's gang in the Yinghuo and Luan areas of Anhui Province, were successively suppressed.

Recently, with the conclusion of the anti-rebellion military campaign and the successive return of troops to the provinces, Xiong submitted a request to the General Headquarters to dissolve the General Headquarters for the Suppression of Bandits in the three provinces. Yesterday, the Headquarters issued a directive stating that during the anti-rebellion military campaign, bandits and communists in the three provinces of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui took the opportunity to secretly cause trouble. Fortunately, the General Commander planned carefully and was able to quell the unrest. Now that the troops have gradually returned, the General Commander is expected to continue his past achievements and strive to suppress the remaining scattered bandits in the three provinces. The request to dissolve the General Headquarters for the Suppression of Bandits is temporarily deferred.

Chinese Shipping Industry Agreed on Methods for Preventing Banditry on River Vessels 177

Banditry Rises in Upper Reaches

Repeated Attempts to Rob Thwarted

Request Warships Patrol to Protect Shipping

Recently, as Chinese ships have begun to resume sailing along the Yangtze River, there have been frequent reports of bandit activity in the upper reaches. River vessels have been shot at and shelled by bandits. Foreign merchant ships have the protection of foreign warships, allowing them to navigate the river, but Chinese ships are in grave danger during this shallow water period. Yesterday, various Chinese river shipping companies in Shanghai, seeking to ensure navigational safety and protect the lives and property of passengers, telegraphed headquarters requesting that the Navy dispatch naval vessels to various locations along the upper reaches to patrol the waterways. The details of this situation are described below:

Bandit Demonstration at Huangsang Estuary: Bandits have resurfaced near the Huangsang Estuary above Daye, aiming to rob merchant ships. These bandits have large numbers and are equipped with guns and cannons. Last week, they opened fire on the Japanese Qing and Taikoo river vessels. Fortunately, these foreign ships were protected by naval personnel and were not successful. The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Jianghua vessel also encountered the same danger while traveling upstream. Yesterday, according to a telegram from the ship's owner, Huang Muzong, the bandits fired eight cannon shots in rapid succession. The ship had no escorting troops, making future voyages extremely dangerous. It is imperative to request the Navy to suppress the bandits, or it will greatly affect navigation.

Upper Yangtze to Suspend Night Navigation: The Taikoo Company's Wuchang vessel also encountered a large group of bandits near Huangzhou. The bandits fired four cannon shots at the ship. Although the ship had naval personnel who fired back with machine guns, the number of bandits was too large, and they were scattered along the river. The ship's captain ordered all lights to be turned off completely to reduce the target for the bandits. The Wuchang vessel was able to escape this danger by traveling quickly through the night. Chinese river vessels traveling on the Upper Yangtze have agreed to temporarily suspend night navigation near Shashi, Chenglingji, and Huangsang Estuary to prevent banditry. This will be until protective measures are in place.

Request for Naval Escort: The owners of the Chinese river vessels, such as the Emei, sailing on the Upper Yangtze, telegraphed Shanghai, stating that the bandits' attempts to rob ships made navigation extremely dangerous. The telegram stated: "Bandits are rampant in the middle reaches of the Yangtze River, and ships traveling up and down the river are frequently shot at or even shelled, making navigation extremely dangerous. Moreover, with the arrival of winter, the water is shallow, and the channels in the Yangtze gorges are constantly changing, causing many ships traveling up and down the river to be afraid to travel at night and must anchor. Without naval protection, it is difficult to find a suitable location, and there is a risk of being kidnapped for ransom. For the sake of the safety of the lives and property of all Chinese and foreign merchants, we request that you forward this request to the headquarters, urging the Navy Department to promptly dispatch several warships to patrol the middle reaches of the Yangtze River, such as the Chenglingji and Shashi areas, and to provide advance notice of naval vessel mooring locations at night and all emergency call signs to facilitate merchant ships approaching the warships and anchoring for protection to avoid danger." (omitted below)

Shipping Merchants Telegraph Government Officials: Shanghai shipping merchants believe that the safety of navigation is crucial to the resumption of regular Chinese river vessel services. Currently, each river vessel only has four officers and soldiers, and their task is to maintain order within the ship rather than preventing banditry. Therefore, the Navy should dispatch warships to suppress bandits along the river to ensure the safety of travelers. Regarding the river vessel owners' request to dispatch warships, it is reported that a telegram has been sent to the National Government requesting that the Navy Department implement this immediately.

The Low-Priced Rice Sales Committee Sells Over 78,000 Shi of Rice 181

Each Shi Loses Approximately 1.4 Yuan

Accounts to be Announced After Meeting

The Municipal Low-Priced Rice Sales Committee, overseen by the Municipal Government, hired people from all walks of life to procure large quantities of rice for sale at low prices to alleviate the living conditions of ordinary people. Ten distribution points were established in the north and south of the city in May of this year, and one was established in each of the rural districts to prevent ordinary people from suffering from high rice prices. By the end of September, the price of rice fell with the arrival of the new rice harvest, and the sales were discontinued. The total amount of rice sold was over 78,000 shi, costing 1.2 million yuan. The total expenses and losses on rice amounted to 110,000 yuan. Each shi lost an average of 1.4 yuan (compared to the historical average of 2 yuan per shi). The loss was covered by a 10,000-yuan subsidy from the Municipal Government and over 23,000 yuan from local grain reserves. The remaining amount was raised by the committee through donations from all walks of life. The committee's accounts are scheduled to be approved and reported at a meeting on the 13th, and the accounts will be formally announced.

Wording to be Amended Today

Contract to be Formally Signed

The case of the seamen requesting a wage increase from various foreign shipping companies has been resolved after previous negotiations. Continued Report on the Shinfong Collision Case 183

The China Merchants Bureau's Shinfong steamer was damaged by the Japanese vessel Keizan Maru at Lutsuchuang, Tanggu, as previously reported. Further details are as follows:

Inspection Upon Arrival in Tianjin: After the collision, the Shinfong steamer sailed to Tianjin. The shipowner, Masun, reported the incident to the Tianjin Customs, which dispatched the River Transportation Department to inspect the vessel. The inspection revealed that the damaged parts were on the upper deck, and the machinery was intact, allowing the ship to continue sailing. However, most of the upper-level cabins were destroyed, so the Customs limited the passenger capacity to fifty-nine people for safety reasons. Cargo could still be loaded.

Departure from Tianjin Today: Yesterday, the Shanghai Bureau received a telegram from shipowner Masun stating that the handling of the matter was proceeding according to instructions. The vessel had salt cargo in Yantai destined for Shanghai, and cabins had been pre-booked. Therefore, the ship had to sail. Today (November 11th), it departed Tianjin for Zhifu, where it will load the salt cargo before returning to Shanghai for major repairs.

Replacement Vessel: The weather in North China is relatively cold, and the Baihe River will soon freeze. Goods are being rushed to Tianjin. Yesterday, the China Merchants Bureau decided that when the Shinfong returns to Shanghai for major repairs, the bureau will assign the Taishun steamer to take over the route. Yesterday, a telegram was sent to the Tianjin Bureau instructing them to continue cargo loading as usual. Simultaneously, local North China cargo brokers were notified.

Navigation Industry Declaration: The Shanghai Navigation Industry's Nine Public Associations Joint Office issued a declaration regarding the collision of the China Merchants Bureau's Shinfong steamer by the Japanese vessel Keizan Maru. The declaration stated that the Shinfong steamer, loaded with cargo and passengers, was sailing twenty li from Tianjin at Lutsuchuang on the evening of the eighth when it was struck by the Keizan Maru, a near-sea steamship of the Japanese Shipping Company, which was departing Tianjin. The Keizan Maru failed to comply with navigation regulations and rammed into the Shinfong, causing severe damage. [China Merchants Bureau's General Manager Li formally notified the company yesterday to negotiate and reserve all loss compensation, etc.] Upon hearing this news, one's hair stands on end in anger. Over the years, Japanese vessels have repeatedly recklessly collided with Chinese ships on rivers and seas, treating human lives as a joke. The New Taming incident from a few years ago remains unresolved, and the families of the victims are still lingering in Shanghai, suffering from cold and hunger. Last year, the Yew Maru sank the New Kang steamer, injuring more than sixty workers. Now, before long, the Shinfong incident has occurred, fully demonstrating their domineering behavior, showing no respect for Chinese people. The lives of our workers on various vessels are also unprotected. In addition to requesting General Manager Li to conduct strict negotiations and forwarding a protest to the central government, this office vows to lead all workers in support, to achieve compensation for losses and guarantees against future incidents.

To protect the lives of workers and prevent such incidents from happening again, it is hoped that all members of the navigation industry will rise up together to provide assistance so that imperialists will be alerted. This will hopefully curb their violent acts in the future. We are filled with deep emotion and earnestly pray for your public consideration.

Local News, Part Two

The Kwang-shih Spinning Machine Invented by a Chinese 186

The Inventor Mr. Kwei-chih Passed Away

The Manager Mr. Kwang-tah is Promoting the Work

Mr. Xing Kwang-shih, from Haimen County, Jiangsu Province, responding to the needs of society and the economy, deduced the principles of artificial spinning in China. After eight years of research, he invented the Kwang-shih spinning machine. The machine is divided into two parts: the carding machine and the yarn drawing machine. The carding machine operates by stepping on the foot pedal to insert raw cotton into the toothed cover, forming batting, which is then rolled into cotton strips and discharged from the machine. The yarn drawing machine works by placing the cotton strip tube on the machine and stepping on the foot pedal. The rotating groove tightens the cotton strip tube with a string, while gears rotate the yarn tube to wrap the yarn, stretching it to form yarn strands. The stretching and twisting occur simultaneously, which is fundamentally different from factory spinning machines. The uneven thickness is adjusted by a safety mechanism, and the thickness of the yarn is controlled by a seven-down, two-hammer system. Yarns ranging from coarse 8-count to fine 30-40 count can be spun by moving the hammer at will. The machine can spin continuously for a long time and is comparable to factory yarn. Overall, the machine's main feature is that it reduces the more than ten steps of factory spinning to two steps, which is a major innovation in the spinning machine industry. Both human and machine power can be used, making it suitable for both households and small factories, which is crucial for the livelihoods of ordinary people. However, just as the machine was about to be assembled, Mr. Xing passed away on October 20th of last year due to overexertion and various stimuli, suffering from cerebral congestion. Currently, Mr. Huang Chang-ting, who collaborated with Mr. Xing at the time, is responsible for managing the machine and is in contact with various parties to continue its development. It is expected that the machine will make a major contribution to the world's textile industry. Here is a record of the inventor Mr. Xing Kwang-shih and the manager Mr. Huang Chang-ting.

Xing Kwang-shih: Mr. Xing's given name was Kwang-shih, courtesy name Pu-wu, also known as Chun-hsien, a native of Haimen County, Jiangsu Province. He graduated from Shanghai Tsing-tsun Normal School and a technical school in his youth. He was skilled at [blank space] and fond of mechanics. At the age of fourteen, he built a bicycle out of wood and could ride it. Later, he imitated Zhuge Liang's wooden ox and flowing horse, creating an iron ox that could carry goods and move, but it still required slight manual propulsion, and it was difficult to maintain balance on uneven ground, so he abandoned it and began studying gravity engines. He used twenty-six gears to add gravity to keep the engine running continuously. However, since one pound of gravity only generated one pound of power and could not multiply it by a thousand or a hundred times, it was ultimately futile but had already taken six years and consumed more than half of his resources. He then turned to studying spinning machines, believing they would be easier to accomplish and would help alleviate poverty. After seven years, he completed wooden 80-spindle yarn drawing and carding machines, but they were not yet perfect. Mr. Xing was a poor scholar, and for more than ten years, he was able to devote himself to mechanics because of the competence of his wife, Madam Ni. However, he was eventually plagued by economic hardship and had to stop. A year later, he met Mr. Chang-ting, who provided financial support to help him continue the project by planning and constructing iron [blank space] 10-spindle yarn drawing and carding machines, which were completed in just over a year. Unexpectedly, just as assembly was about to be completed, Mr. Xing succumbed to the exhaustion of poverty and hardship, dying on October 20th, 1929, at the age of only forty-one.

Huang Chang-ting: Huang Chang-ting, courtesy name [blank space] Yi, is a native of Haimen County, Jiangsu Province, aged thirty-two. He graduated from National Nanjing Higher Normal School and Southeast University. Through a relative or friend, he met Mr. Xing because he was really constrained to interrupt the development of his spinning machine.

Photograph of the Kwang-shih Spinning Machine 187

The upper right corner shows the photograph of the inventor, Mr. Xing Kwang-shih, and the upper left corner shows the photograph of the manager, Mr. Huang Chang-ting.

At that time, Mr. Xing had other [blank space] in Luoyang and resigned. He resolutely collaborated with Mr. Xing, with Mr. Xing in charge of manufacturing and Mr. Huang in charge of finances and planning. However, his family was poor and had no savings, so he sold his property and borrowed money to barely make ends meet. After Mr. Xing died and had no money for his funeral, Mr. Huang managed his funeral and educated his orphaned children, continuing the development of the machine. All of this depended on Mr. Huang's planning and management, and his perseverance is admirable.

An Adventure of a Fishing Boat 189

Sixteen Boatmen in Total

Drifted for a Day and a Night

Fortunately Rescued by a Fishing Boat

The Cargo is Missing

The large fishing boat Jin Shuntai, loaded with 5,000 pieces of timber, over 1,000 loads of green charcoal, and other miscellaneous goods from Wenzhou, Fujian Province, was sailing into the Yangtze River to unload its cargo. At about 5:00 AM the day before yesterday, while sailing through the Tongsha waters off the coast of Wusong, a hurricane suddenly arose on the sea, and the waves were surging. The boat could not move forward and was soon submerged by a huge wave. The sixteen crew members on board saw that the boat was doomed and that they would become denizens of the deep. They were terrified and quickly cut down the canvas of the main mast. The crew members all hid under the canvas and drifted with the waves for a day and a night. In the vast ocean, there was no shore in sight. It was about 7:00 AM the next day (yesterday) that the boatmen, who had lost all hope of survival, were in dire straits. Fortunately, a fishing boat from Dayangshan passed by and noticed them. They rushed to rescue them, and all sixteen crew members were saved, but they were all on the verge of death. After being resuscitated, they gradually regained consciousness. The crew members then took a small sailboat to Wusong at about 5:00 PM yesterday to report to the water police and request that they investigate the whereabouts of the cargo.

The Murderer in the Funing Case Was Arrested in Shanghai 190

Claimed to Have Fled to Shanghai After the Murder

Two Suspects Were Detained by the Police After Eating Lunch

Cui Changsheng, a native of Funing, lived in the forty-eight rooms of Nanyang Bridge. His cousin, Yang Tianxiang, was a 22-year-old farmer who had some savings. On the 29th of last month, he was suddenly murdered, and the murderer fled without a trace. Cui was in Shanghai and did not know about this matter until he received a letter from his uncle, Yang Bingfa, on the 9th, in which he learned the details. The letter stated that his second son, Tianxiang, was shot dead on the 29th by Wei Qin-zhi, Yang Bingqian, Li Yu-chen, Xu Guowu, Yang Weixing, etc. The county government has been petitioned to conduct an autopsy and arrest the murderer. It is heard that the murderer has fled to Shanghai, so please be vigilant in investigating the case and avenging the injustice. Cui Changsheng was originally acquainted with Yang Weixing and others when he was in his hometown, so after receiving the letter, he paid close attention to the investigation. At first, Cui met Yang Weifeng on Beiler Road in the French Concession on the morning of the 9th. Yang said that he had fled to Shanghai because he had committed a murder in his hometown. However, at that time, Cui Changsheng had not yet received the letter from his uncle and did not pay attention to Yang's words. Cui was shocked when he received the letter that afternoon and went to inquire, but he did not meet Yang. Yesterday morning, he met Yang Weixing on Shanxi Road again and pretended not to know about the murder case, inviting Yang to lunch at a restaurant at the Baoshan Road intersection. Cui then persuaded Yang to invite Yang Bingqian to go together. After arriving in the Chinese territory, Cui immediately called the police to detain the two Yangs at the fifth district public security bureau on Baoshan Road. Yang Weixing, 29 years old, from Funing, served as the village chief. He claimed that he came to Shanghai on the 11th to treat his eye disease and lived on Pingji Road in the French Concession. Yang Bingqian, 25 years old, from Funing, served as the deputy village chief. He came to Shanghai on the 13th to treat his hemorrhoids and lived on Shanxi Road. Both denied the murder case of Yang Tianxiang and claimed that Yang Tianxiang had a conflict with Wei Qin-zhi, the patrol chief of the sixth police station of the fifth branch of the Funing County Public Security Bureau, over the collection of land taxes and was shot to death. The plaintiff, Cui Changsheng, has now sent a telegram to Funing requesting that they come and take the suspects away.

Bandit Ting Chin-fang Sentenced to Death for Kidnapping 191

Detective Shang Wu of the Huishi Patrol Room previously arrested four bandits: Ting Chin-fang, Wang Kuo-liang, Yang Lien-en, and Chen Miao-ching. It was found that Ting kidnapped Zhou Tsung-chih, the accountant of the Hong Yu Cotton Yarn Company on Dagu Road, at 9:15 AM on January 14th of last year, and demanded ransom. Wang and Yang were involved in writing threatening letters to Shao Yen-shan, the manager of the Tung Yu Money Exchange on Tianjin Road. Chen was suspected of helping the criminals escape. They were sent to the Special District Local Court for interrogation. The court has now reached a verdict, which was announced by Judge Sun Yuan in the Second Criminal Court yesterday morning. The main text of the verdict states that Ting Chin-fang is sentenced to death for kidnapping and demanding ransom, and deprived of his civil rights for life. Wang Kuo-liang is sentenced to two years of imprisonment for attempted extortion and two years of imprisonment for possessing military weapons, with the sentences to be served concurrently for a total of two years and two months. The number of days of detention before the final judgment can be used to offset the imprisonment at a rate of two days for one day. Yang Lien-en and Chen Miao-ching are found not guilty. Yang and Chen each submitted a bond of 500 yuan and one confiscated pistol during the appeal period.

Ferry Operators at Muddy Ford Request Designation of a Wharf 193

Ferry operators Li Ching-hua and Lu San-san of Pudong's Muddy Ford submitted a document to the Shanghai Municipal Fifth District Party Department, stating that the livelihood of the ferry operators is dependent on maintaining their business, and requesting that the Municipal Government be consulted to designate a ferry wharf for permanent use. It is learned that Ching-hua's original Muddy Ford ferry service was converted into a municipal ferry by the Municipal Public Works Bureau, and their livelihood was in jeopardy. They previously requested that the department take measures to provide relief. Having read in the newspaper that the Municipal Government had responded to the Municipal Party Department, the Municipal Government stated that the original Muddy Ford ferry service would still be allowed to continue operating and that the location of the ferry and the ferry service would not conflict. This inclusive representation of the municipal government is out of the department's intent to protect the livelihood of the people. Ching-hua and others are deeply grateful for the benefits they have received. However, the Muddy Justice Wharf that Ching-hua and others are currently using and the Tungchang Wharf designated by the Municipal Public Works Bureau for the municipal ferry are both located on private land owned by the Yu family. In 1927, the landowner Yu Chih-ching discontinued the Muddy Justice Wharf for usage relation of the land and changed the discharging site to the Tungchang Wharf. A request has been submitted to the former Tanggong Bureau. However, for some reason, it was not implemented. The Tungchang Wharf has now been designated as a ferry wharf by the Municipal Public Works Bureau.

Page 16

If the Yu family landowner insists on reclaiming the discontinued Muddy Justice Wharf, then the ferry service of Ching-hua and others will inevitably follow the same path as the municipal ferry. The ferry and ferry service operating in the same location will naturally not leave any room for the ferry service to stand. In order to determine the location of the ferry wharf, Ching-hua and others have applied to the Municipal Public Works Bureau to investigate the archives and designate the Muddy Justice Wharf currently used by Ching-hua and others or other suitable locations as a permanent wharf for the ferry service, so that the livelihood of dozens of families can be protected. The livelihoods of dozens of families are all dependent on the relief efforts of the department. They still earnestly hope that it will be maintained throughout and that the Municipal Government will be consulted to order the Municipal Public Works Bureau to quickly designate a permanent ferry wharf to protect the livelihoods of dozens of families in Ching-hua and others. This would truly be a benevolent act. Respectfully submitted to the Shanghai Municipal Fifth District Party Department.

Du Yuesheng Supports the National Products Market 194

Mr. Zhang Zilian has been actively promoting national goods after establishing the Chinese National Products Market at the Municipal Hall on Nanjing Road. Mr. Du Yuesheng, who is enthusiastic about public welfare, praised this endeavor and will purchase land in the South City to build a building and open a national goods department store to support Mr. Zhang. Municipal Public Works Bureau Improves Coal Used in Power Plant Boilers 195

Prompting the Abolition of Coal Contracting Methods

The Municipal Public Works Bureau believes that boiler coal is a major expenditure for the power plant. Whether it is burned economically is directly related to the cost and indirectly affects electricity prices. It is necessary to pay special attention to this. It is now found that the boiler coal used by the China Electric Company has been using coal contracting methods for many years. Everything is entrusted to the contracted coal company without any investigation. Whether the quality of coal and the amount of coal used are commensurate with the contracted price has not been calculated, and it is impossible to investigate whether the burning is economical. Moreover, the company's boiler equipment will soon be [blank space]. The amount of coal used will increase in the future, making coal contracting methods even more unsuitable. The company is therefore ordered to abolish the coal contracting system as soon as possible in order to calculate costs and improve efficiency.

General Overview of Construction in the City in October 196

This month, the Municipal Public Works Bureau issued 152 construction permits, 102 repair permits, 112 miscellaneous permits, and 23 demolition permits. Compared with last month, the number of construction, repair, and demolition permits decreased slightly, while the number of miscellaneous permits increased slightly. Compared with the same month last year, the number of repair permits decreased slightly, while the number of demolition permits increased slightly. The number of construction permits increased by about one-sixth, and the number of miscellaneous permits increased by about one-quarter. The total construction area in the city, excluding rural bungalows, is about 4,380 square feet, an increase of 220 square feet compared to last month. The estimated value is about 1.16 million yuan, a decrease of more than 350,000 yuan compared to last month, probably due to the increase in the number of bungalows and the decrease in the number of multi-story buildings. By district, South Shanghai still ranks first. Huahua District jumped to second place due to more construction projects, while Zhabei ranked third. Larger projects include four in South Shanghai, one in Zhabei, and one in Huahua: (1) The city is building affordable housing on Xietu Road, covering an area of 650 square feet, with an estimated value of 85,000 yuan. (2) The owner, Chen Sijiang, is building two two-story buildings and a two-story bathhouse on Chunghua Road, covering a total area of 40 square feet, with an estimated value of 70,040 yuan. (3) The owner, Cen Junheng, is building 22 houses on Chuan Highway, covering an area of 100 square feet, with an estimated value of 40,000 yuan. (4) The Inland Cotton Co., Ltd. is building a weaving factory on Robertson Road, covering an area of 1,090 square feet, with an estimated value of 196,000 yuan. The area of old houses demolished is 1,175 square feet, a decrease of about 1,000 square feet compared to last month, but still about the same as in August. Enforcement Matters: There were 122 enforcement matters this month, slightly more than last month and about one-third more than the same month last year. Dangerous Houses Ordered to be Demolished: There are 221 dangerous houses throughout the city. As of the end of this month, 150 have been demolished, and 71 are still being urged to be demolished.

Results of Ningbo Lawyers' Investigation of the Xin Dingxiang Case 199

After the sampan worker Xin Dingxiang was pushed into the Huangpu River and drowned by French sailors, various labor unions and hometown associations in this city organized a Xin Case Support Association, distributed declarations, and invited more than twenty Ningbo lawyers to discuss the legal issues of the Xin case in order to petition the Ministry of Foreign Affairs for legal negotiations and to protect national dignity. Yesterday, the lawyers reported the results of their investigation of the case to the Ningbo Hometown Association in Shanghai, stating: [After the colleagues questioned Zhu Gengsheng, Ge Amao, and Xin Siyuan, etc., who witnessed the incident at the Shanghai Ningbo Hometown Association on November 2nd of this year, the colleagues jointly investigated the facts of this case (1) The two French sailors should have given Xin Dingxiang the boat fare, but they refused to pay, the fault was on their side first (2) Xin Dingxiang was standing at the bow of the sampan, if he was pushed, there was a possibility he would drown and die, anyone could recognize the danger of the result, according to the law, the French sailors violently pushed Xin Dingxiang into the water causing him to drown and die, their actions have the suspicion of intentional homicide, as for what happened after the incident, the 415 Indian constables and the Western constables of the water patrol station released the French sailors who were suspected of murder without pursuing them according to law, there is also the suspicion of dereliction of duty, this matter concerns the national dignity and the lives of the people, therefore, we dare to report the results of the investigation as follows (attached three pieces of draft statements from Xin Siyuan, Zhu Gengsheng, and Ge Amao) Investigation report by lawyers Wei Tong, Dai Chengxiang, Hu Fenglian, Hu Jun'an, Chen Ziyu, Liu Lailiang, Shan Junren]

It is also reported that after the investigation report of the Xin case, it is planned to organize an expanded publicity meeting to convey to all domestic organizations to support it unanimously, and to ask overseas Chinese and translate it into English to send to various countries for public opinion.

Last autumn, the Chinese Women's Temperance Association launched a fundraising campaign to expand its beggar relief efforts. Besides a portion of this fund being used for the current year's expenses of the Reformatory, the rest is planned to be used to build a Maternal Love Dormitory behind Yunfang Hall, specifically for accommodating women with young children who are among the beggars being reformed, in order to align with the association's purpose of protecting children and promoting motherhood. Taxpayers' Association Supports Concession's Gambling Ban 201

Yesterday, the Shanghai Concession Chinese Taxpayers' Association sent a letter to Mr. Edwards, the General Manager of the Shanghai Municipal Council, stating: Respected Sir, having investigated the harms of gambling to the common people, the creation of all kinds of evils, and the administrative experience and common sense that everyone knows, this Association detests gambling as an enemy and has actively attacked and requested the Council to ban the dog racing gambling since the beginning until now. Now, Council Chairman Mr. Fessenden and Chief Inspector Mr. Qu Jide share the same opinion on anti-gambling as this Association and proposed to first ban dog racing gambling, but the operators of the dog racing track published a rebuttal in the newspaper, as if gambling is a business that the people of civilized countries should have and placed the responsibility of permission on the Council. Fortunately, the Council corrected its mistake and did not prioritize the interests of a few people over the interests of all residents. Chairman Fessenden made a statement today declaring that a gambling ban is imperative. This Association firmly believes that at the Council meeting at 4:30 PM tomorrow, regarding the ban on dog racing gambling, in addition to Director Hua Chongri naturally supporting it unanimously, the remaining British and American Directors, if they are not shareholders or related to the dog racing track, will definitely base their decision on their administrative experience and common sense and will also support it unanimously, otherwise, they will not be able to call themselves people of civilized countries. Correspondingly, this letter is sent in the hope that you will review it and request that the Council unanimously decide to ban gambling and express respect to Chairman Fessenden on your behalf.

Fines for Not Affixing Stamps 202

Tianfuhao Repeated Offense, Fined Double, 40 Yuan

The Remaining Six Shops Fined 30 Yuan Each

Tianfu Nanhua Shop on Great Horse Road was found to be evading stamp duty by using disguised invoices and had been previously fined. Six shops including Tianbao Shop on Second Horse Road, Gongli Sock Factory on Great Horse Road, Dekang Wood Shop on Yalu Road, etc., were all sued by the Municipal Council's lawyer for not affixing stamps to their invoices. Yesterday (November 11th) at 9 AM, Magistrate Tao Dejun of the Special District Court presided over the trial. The court ruled that Tianfu Nanhua Shop had intentionally repeated the offense and was fined double, 40 yuan. Tianbao Shop, Gongli Sock Factory, and the other six shops were each fined 30 yuan. Ruixiang Electrical Supplies Shop, Xiuse Xiangjia, and Shenhe Store were rescheduled for trial on the 15th of this month because they did not appear.

Ministry Orders Attention to Ham Shipped to Hong Kong and Macau 207

Must Undergo Pre-Slaughter and Post-Slaughter Inspection

Before Being Allowed to be Shipped to Hong Kong and Macau for Sale

The Ministry of Industry and Commerce stated that recently, according to the report of the China Ham Joint Company, in recent months, ham from our country has often been transshipped through Hong Kong, Macau, Qingdao, and other places to be gradually loaded to the Philippine Islands, a territory of China. This ham is not only not subject to legal pre-slaughter and post-slaughter inspection, but is mostly inferior goods on the market for profit. At a time when American meat merchants are resisting the import of our country's meat merchants, it is feared that once this unsanitary ham is inspected by the Philippine government, it will inevitably issue a ban, affecting international trade, which is no small matter. For this reason, it is appealed to consult the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to negotiate with the authorities in Hong Kong and Macau to strictly investigate and prohibit it, and to order the Qingdao Customs and local authorities to investigate and prohibit it in order to solidify the position of international trade. After receiving the report, the Ministry of Industry and Commerce stated that the shipping of ham to the Philippine Islands has special circumstances. Previously, it had ordered the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau that from July of this year, ham made from legs that have undergone pre-slaughter and post-slaughter inspection can be shipped for sale. Now, it orders the Bureau again that in the future, attention should be paid to ham shipped to Hong Kong and Macau.

Verdict to Be Announced in Case of Auto Striking and Killing Vietnamese Constable 208

Appraiser Has Submitted Report

Vietnamese constable No. 398 of the French Concession police station was on duty at the intersection of Route Sayzoong and Rue Massenet in July when a car No. 1873 driven by Yu Xinkui, a driver of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, and a car No. 2377 driven by Sun Zulin, a driver of Sun Baorong, a councilor of the Municipal Government, collided with each other, injuring and killing the constable. Afterwards, the police station brought the two parties to the French court for several trials, and the court ordered personnel to investigate the circumstances of the incident at that time before reviewing the case. Yesterday, another trial was held. First, Mr. Teppak, the lawyer representing Yu Xinkui, stated that the appraiser's report now proves that his client was not at fault. At that time, the accident was caused by Sun Zulin's car driving from south to north at excessive speed, so it is difficult to shirk the blame for causing this disaster. At that time, his client's car was damaged by Sun's car, and the repair cost was estimated to be 280 taels. In addition, since the car was hit, it could not be driven and was detained by the police station. The car owner hired another car for use, and the loss was estimated to be 1,000 taels, which he requested to be compensated for in total. Mr. Bahr, the lawyer representing Sun Zulin, stated that after his lawyer observed the appraiser's report, the words were all one-sided. According to the actual situation at the time, Yu Xinkui's car was speeding, causing his client's car to be unable to brake and stop, causing the accident. His client was not at fault, and the blame was on the other party. He requested a public judgment. The Chinese and Western officials announced the end of the debate and listened to the review and judgment.

Teenager Attempts Suicide by Drowning in Cold Weather 209

Trembling After Being Rescued

There Were Two Reasons for the Suicide

Yesterday afternoon at around 1 PM, a teenager wearing a military uniform with a military belt, resembling a junior officer, was wandering around the Renji Road pier on the north bank of the Suzhou Creek. Suddenly, he walked to the edge of the pier and jumped into the river to commit suicide. Fortunately, the 31st and 67th Chinese constables of the water patrol station were patrolling the river and immediately took measures to rescue him. At that time, the weather was very cold, and the teenager was drenched and shivering. After being taken back to the police station and changing into dry clothes, he claimed that his name was Sun Deyuan, and he came from the military. Because he was disappointed in love and suffered economic pressure, he took this desperate path. His father's name is Sun Weiwen, and he lives at No. 405 Yaofu Lane, Hankou Road. The head constable ordered Chinese detective Cheng Yongnian to go to the address to inform his father, who arrived at the police station and returned home with Sun.

Japan's Trade with China in October 210

Totaled 32 Million Yuan

With an Export Surplus of 21 Million Yuan

Yesterday, the Japanese Commercial Counselor's Office in this city received a telegram from its home country stating that the total amount of Japanese-Chinese exports in October was 32 million Japanese yen, and the export surplus (that is, the import deficit from our country's perspective) accounted for 21 million yuan. Also, from January to October, Japan's export surplus in trade with China totaled 92 million yuan, but this was 59 million yuan less than in the same period last year. As for Japan's total foreign trade, exports in October totaled 128 million yuan, with an export surplus of 26 million yuan. However, the total foreign trade for the ten months of this year is still an import deficit of 115 million yuan, which is 22 million yuan more than in the same period last year. If there were no export surplus in trade with China to offset it, the total import surplus would reach more than 200 million yuan.

Esperanto Scholar Beeler Arrives in Shanghai 211

Has Traveled Over 30,000 Miles

Esperanto scholar Beeler, who is only twenty-four years old, set off from Lyon, France, on July 24, 1928, riding a bicycle eastward through Central Asia and into Soviet Russia, then to Japan, where he stayed for three months. Now he has arrived in Shanghai on the Nagasaki Maru. According to Mr. Beeler, he has traveled more than 20,000 miles since he set off. He encountered many dangers when he passed through Central Asia, but fortunately he was safe. The purpose of this trip is to promote Esperanto. He achieved great results in Japan for several months. Now that he has come to Shanghai, he is willing to discuss Esperanto with comrades in Shanghai who speak Esperanto and to tell them about his travels. He also said that there is another comrade named Schlier who can arrive in Shanghai by Green Shirt steamer today. He will cooperate with him to study and promote the method of Esperanto. As for how long Mr. Beeler will stay in Shanghai, he himself cannot predict. After leaving Shanghai in the future, he plans to go to Vietnam, the Straits Settlements, Australia, etc., and then return to China via the Americas.

Central Bank Inspection Report 212

Seventy-First Time

The 71st Central Bank Issuance Reserve Inspection Report states: In accordance with the provisions of Article 15 of the Central Bank Regulations, this Association is responsible for inspecting the reserve funds for the issuance of exchange coupons by the Bank. Now, on November 10th of the 19th year of the Republic of China, the 71st inspection was held at the Bank's Issuance Bureau, and the inspection results are announced as follows: The total amount of exchange coupons issued is 22,058,812 silver dollars, including 11,122,412 silver dollar coupons and 12-fold auxiliary coin coupons of 936,400 silver dollars. The total amount of exchange coupon reserve funds is 22,058,812 yuan, including 19,525,452 yuan in cash reserve in silver dollars. The cash reserve includes 15,008,494.27 yuan stored in the Bank's Issuance Vault, 1,322,217 yuan stored in branch banks in various ports, and 3,194,740.73 yuan stored with peer banks. The collateral reserve is converted into silver dollars according to Article 2 of the Central Bank Exchange Coupon Regulations, with 60% in cash reserve and 40% in collateral reserve. The inspection results show that the cash exceeds 60% and the collateral is less than 40%, which is in line with the regulations. This report is hereby made. Li Fuxun, Chairman of the Board of Supervisors of the Central Bank of the Republic of China, November 10th, 17th Year, Supervisor Gong Jingli, Bei Songsun, Qin Runqing, Yu Qiaqing, Lin Kanghou, Xu Jifei.
